  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3d5deb6f-d9a0-49de-b426-987d7d54fc83'
      });

  <span id="freeText8536560979221814551" style="display:none">Since birth, Nyx has been betrothed to the evil ruler of her kingdom-all because of a foolish bargain struck by her father. And since birth, she has been in training to kill him.<br /><br />With no choice but to fulfill her duty, Nyx resents her family for never trying to save her and hates herself for wanting to escape her fate. Still, on her seventeenth birthday, Nyx abandons everything she's ever known to marry the all-powerful, immortal Ignifex. Her plan? Seduce him, destroy his enchanted castle, and break the nine-hundred-year-old curse he put on her people.<br /><br />But Ignifex is not at all what Nyx expected. The strangely charming lord beguiles her, and his castle—a shifting maze of magical rooms—enthralls her.<br /><br />As Nyx searches for a way to free her homeland by uncovering Ignifex's secrets, she finds herself unwillingly drawn to him. Even if she could bring herself to love her sworn enemy, how can she refuse her duty to kill him? With time running out, Nyx must decide what is more important: the future of her kingdom, or the man she was never supposed to love.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_20622698').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_20622698').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/34125767-nikolae-keaveney"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1486325422i/34125767._UX100_CR0,14,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/34125767-nikolae-keaveney">Nikolae Keaveney</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    HEAVY SPOILERS<br />HEAVY SPOILERS<br />HEAVY SPOILERS<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Okay. i just read it and the ending confused me as well. But I'm going to try anyways.<br />Shade+Ignifex=Lux (the<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    HEAVY SPOILERS<br />HEAVY SPOILERS<br />HEAVY SPOILERS<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Okay. i just read it and the ending confused me as well. But I'm going to try anyways.<br />Shade+Ignifex=Lux (the last prince who everyone thought died). Everyone in Arcadia thought that the last prince was killed by the Gentle Lord. NO, it's a lie. The prince was too scared to fail the kindly ones' test that he bargained with them to not kill him and protect his kingdom. But the kindly ones (the nasty ones in my opinion) tricked him and locked his entire country into permanent darkness. Then the they proceeded to change Lux into Shade and Ignifex, lock them both into the castle, where they have to stay for an eternity. <br />Nyx let the children of Typhon to attack Ignifex so he and Shade can combine into the prince. Then the prince opened the jar (which contained the entire kingdom), and rewinded time, freeing the country from demons but locking himself into the darkness of the jar forever. <br />Nyx woke up one morning and thought she had a bad dream. Everything was fuzzy but she had this weird feeling that something had happened. When she was about to marry TOM-A-LONE, she suddenly remembered what happened. <br />Okay, this is the confusing part. When Nyx woke up, technically the 900 years of demons had never happened, because time had been unwounded by the prince. That is why she couldn't remember anything. So the events she experienced in her life and her love Ignifex had never existed. However, because the prince unwounded time, he also locked himself permanently into the darkness of the jar. He was stuck in the castle.<br />Nyx rushed to the castle, saw the prince coming with the kindly ones, and tried to bargain with them. She wanted to free the prince, but nothing can exchange his freedom. Finally she said that she would stay with him in the darkness of the jar. The kindly ones laughed at her and agreed. <br />So the duet suffered through the darkness, and was saved by their own heart. Because both Nyx and Lux had kindness in their heart, and the kindly ones valued the moral so much.<br />So they were free!<br />YAY!<br />I hope this answered your question.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Ignifex is described in the book as extremely attractive despite his cat-like red eyes. He has high cheekbones, a strong jawline, and he has long blac<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Ignifex is described in the book as extremely attractive despite his cat-like red eyes. He has high cheekbones, a strong jawline, and he has long black hair. It's not a typical "Beauty and the Beast"-esque story. He's beautiful, but beastly in the sense that he is a "bad" man. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_795460503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/795460503" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/795460503?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer795460503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6468212320138692331"><b>Well, I thought this was wonderful.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389124061i/7992415.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty' title='Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cruel Beauty</a>?<br/><br/>• It's a gorgeously written blend of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling and Greek mythology.<br/>• It's at once a powerful, wonderful, heart-breaking love story and so so much more than that.<br/>• It's a dark tale that stabs you in the heart at every turn and constantly throws all new levels of craziness into the mix.<br/>• And it's the latest addition to my favourite YA of all time shelf.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty' title='Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cruel Beauty</a> shouldn't work. But somehow it does. It managed to have m</span>
  <span id="freeText6468212320138692331" style="display:none"><b>Well, I thought this was wonderful.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389124061i/7992415.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a>?<br><br>• It's a gorgeously written blend of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling and Greek mythology.<br>• It's at once a powerful, wonderful, heart-breaking love story and so so much more than that.<br>• It's a dark tale that stabs you in the heart at every turn and constantly throws all new levels of craziness into the mix.<br>• And it's the latest addition to my favourite YA of all time shelf.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a> shouldn't work. But somehow it does. It managed to have me on the edge of my seat from start to finish. It shocked me. It creeped me out. I laughed. I cried. I'm still not sure I understand the ending but I am sure that it doesn't really matter. In short, I loved it. It was one of those rare books that literally glued my eyes to the page, had me devouring each sentence in a mad need to find out what the hell was going on and what would happen. It was a bizarrely beautiful little addiction and I only hope this signifies the start of a great year for young adult (after the last was so disappointing).<br><br>So... Nyx. The best books are held aloft by a great protagonist and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a> is no exception. Nyx is exactly the kind of character I love. She's strong-willed, witty and brave. She's also angry, bitter and ferocious. She's lived her whole life being prepared as a weapon; and as a sacrifice. Her father made a deal with the Gentle Lord - the evil ruler of their kingdom - before Nyx and her twin sister were born. Their mother had been unable to conceive a child, so their father foolishly asked that the Lord grant them children and promised one of his daughters to the Lord in exchange. But he also lost his wife to childbirth in the bargain. The Gentle Lord's habit of cashing in double on his deals is well-known. Nyx, as the child her father loved less, has long-known her destiny to be the wife of the Gentle Lord. When the times comes, she goes with determination, fear and anger. She does not play by the Lord's rules. She is defiant. She tests his patience. I liked her instantly.<br><br>Then there is Ignifex, of course. The Lord that has terrorized their kingdom for centuries. The one who carries the blood of countless innocents on his hands. But, unsurprisingly, things are never quite that simple. What I liked best about Ignifex was his wicked sense of humour. There's nothing quite like a villain who is constantly witty and hilarious. The complex layers of each character in this book just blew my mind, no one is ever simple or cliche. The heroine does plenty of bad things and the evil villain... well, be careful you don't fall in love.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a> was just so unexpected. I thought I knew exactly what it was as soon as I glimpsed the cover, title and GR description. I thought I understood perfectly and I thought I'd probably read countless versions of the same book. <b>How wrong I was</b>. This is honestly quite unlike anything I've ever read before. I liked how everything about the book, the setting, the story and the characters was a bit like one of those Russian dolls. Something else within something else within something else. Then there's that whole haunting bittersweet tone that permeates this entire novel. I swear Ms Hodge has perfected the art of raising goosebumps with a perfectly-spun twist on an old Greek myth. And it just got better and better. <br><br>I think this review is more of an incoherent mess of feelings, so I'll stop now before the drooling starts. <b>What I want to know is this: when is the author releasing another book?</b><br><br><br><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/emilymay" rel="nofollow noopener">Leafmarks</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6468212320138692331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1308410945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3176591882068107779">I don’t know if Cruel Beauty truly deserved five stars on merit but goddamnit I’m awarding it all the points for enjoyability. All of them. I loved the hell out of this story. The passion. The intrigue. Ignifex. Nyx’s rage. Ignifex. All the kissing. Nyx.<br/><br/>This book kind of had it all for me. Plot, mystery, intrigue and a whole lot of making out. It’s almost like Hodge was trying to distract me from the crazy plotholes and loose story structure. It was fantastic! I haven’t been this entertained by </span>
  <span id="freeText3176591882068107779" style="display:none">I don’t know if Cruel Beauty truly deserved five stars on merit but goddamnit I’m awarding it all the points for enjoyability. All of them. I loved the hell out of this story. The passion. The intrigue. Ignifex. Nyx’s rage. Ignifex. All the kissing. Nyx.<br /><br />This book kind of had it all for me. Plot, mystery, intrigue and a whole lot of making out. It’s almost like Hodge was trying to distract me from the crazy plotholes and loose story structure. It was fantastic! I haven’t been this entertained by a book in ages. I immediately went out and bought a copy (I got mine from the library).<br /><br />So if you’re into mythology and kissing and just looking for something eminently, page-turningly good, then this is your book.<br /><br />This is only a mini review as I wrote a guide to Beauty and the Beast retellings <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2015/06/25/a-comprehensive-look-at-beauty-and-the-beast-retellings" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_646300881" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646300881" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646300881?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=twins-triplets-clones">twins-triplets-clones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alternate-retelling">alternate-retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alternate-universe">alternate-universe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646300881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9652936156943143748"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If one of us had to die, it ought to be the one with poison in her heart.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>Actual rating: 3.5<br/><br/>Maybe it's just me, but I've rarely encountered a <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling that I haven't loved. Ok, except <i>Beastly</i>. That abomination was just horrible all the way around. And let's not even mention the movie. Some people just have the kind of face that just begs for an encounter with my fist, and pretty boy Pettyfer is one of them. But I digress.<br/><br/>This was a very enjoyable read, though not</span>
  <span id="freeText9652936156943143748" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If one of us had to die, it ought to be the one with poison in her heart.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>Actual rating: 3.5<br /><br />Maybe it's just me, but I've rarely encountered a <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling that I haven't loved. Ok, except <i>Beastly</i>. That abomination was just horrible all the way around. And let's not even mention the movie. Some people just have the kind of face that just begs for an encounter with my fist, and pretty boy Pettyfer is one of them. But I digress.<br /><br />This was a very enjoyable read, though not without its faults. It is supposed to be a retelling of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, but I felt like it had hints of the fairy tales <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i> and <i>Bluekbeard</i> as well. I can go on for days about the plot, setting, grammatical structure blah blah blah, but let's be honest, what makes or breaks a book is its narrator. If you don't like the narrator, screw the rest of the book; <b>I really liked this book's main character, Nyx</b>.<br /><br />I like my heroines flawed, strong, and strong-willed. I like it when they're angry. I like it when they're defiant. I like it when they lose control. I like it when they snap like a rubber band strung past its tautness. I like it when they see their own weakness. I love it when they fall apart. I love it when they hurt someone they love, while hating themselves for it because they are past their breaking point. Nyx is strong, but not to the point where her overwhelming bitchiness eclipse the book; she never, ever, ever comes off as bitchy.<br /><br />I do have a few problems with Nyx, and my problem with her ties into the plot as well, <b>my main complaint about this book is that it is just overwhelmingly romantic at times</b>. "But Khanh!" you protest, "It's a romance novel, I mean, it's based off a fairy tale, what did you fucking expect?" Well, yes, my friends, it is a fairy-tale, but the premise promised me more than that. It promised me intrigue, it promised me a kick-ass heroine, one who is the savior of her people, one who will sacrifice herself and become a killer of an evil immortal. I didn't exactly get that.<br /><br />I wanted bad-assery. I wanted more plotting. <b>I wanted an assassin. Instead, I got not a lot of plotting, I got a lot of illicit kissing, I got a lot of falling in love.</b> As beautiful as this book was, it felt to me that the MAIN plot of mayhem and murder got tossed aside for a love triangle. It wasn't exactly <i>Throne of Glass</i> bad, but it bothered me a lot the way Nyx skirted her mission for romance and dreams. In terms of plotting, the second half of the book was a big mess of confusion for me.<br /><br /><u>The Summary</u>: Some people are born to a grand destiny, others have it forced upon them. Nyx was born to be a sacrifice. Demons have control of the country of Arcadia. There is no sun, there is only a parchment paper sky, painted with an artifice of the sun. Her country lives in fear. To gaze upon the demons is to lose your mind as the shadows prey upon your soul. For 900 years, this has been Arcadia's curse.<br /><br />Nyx was intended by her father to be the savior of her people. It means she will most definitely die. Her father made a deal with the king of the demons, the Gentle Lord; in exchange, Nyx will be given in marriage to the Gentle Lord when she turns 17. In return, her beloved twin sister, Astraia, will be able to live a normal, happy life. Nyx truly loves her twin sister, the innocent, sweet Astraia, but it is so hard not to feel resentment at one who has been the recipient of all their father's love, while knowing that her happiness will come at the cost of your own, but she is determined to fulfil her mission:<blockquote>
  <i>I had broken my sister’s heart. I would never see her again, so I could never beg her forgiveness. I had let hatred fester in me so long, I didn’t think I could ever learn to love her properly, either. But I could make sure she lived free of the Gentle Lord, no longer afraid of his demons, with the true sun shining down upon her.</i>
</blockquote>Nyx has been groomed half her life to be the Gentle Lord's bride, but her father and his secret society has other plans for her: <b>she will marry him, she will seduce him, she will kill him</b>. Nyx will save Arcadia from the demons.<br /><br />The Gentle Lord is not what she expected. He tells her to call her Ignifex, but that's not his true name. Instead of ravishing her, he leaves her in a tenuous peace. He has but two rules for her (which are so reminiscent to me of <i>Rumpelstiltskin</i> and <i>Blackbeard</i>): <blockquote>
  <i>"One. Every night I will offer you the chance to guess my name. If you guess right, you have your freedom. If you guess wrong, you die.”<br /><br />"Rule two. Most of the doors in this house are locked. This key will open all the rooms you are permitted to enter. Do not try to enter the other rooms or you will regret it dearly...though not for very long.”</i>
</blockquote>Instead of someone unimaginably cruel, the stuff of nightmares, she finds him full of laughter, full of mockery, full of games. He likes her spirit, he likes her defiance.<blockquote>
  <i>I do like a wife with a little malice in her heart.</i>
</blockquote>But Ignifex is also capable of unimaginable cruelty; he makes her shudder with fear. Unexpectedly, she finds an ally in his magical castle, one named Shade. One who is close to the Gentle Lord, but who can never betray him.<br /><br />Who can Nyx trust?<br /><br /><u>The Setting</u>: Interesting...but it didn't quite work for me. The setting is not the star here, and it's a rather vague alternative universe that is rather jarring at times. It is based off of an ancient Greco-Roman world, as far as I can tell, gods and goddesses in the Greek Pantheon such as Aphrodite and Hermes and Zeus are mentioned, and it seems as if they are part of the traditional belief system. There is a vague system of magic, alchemy of sort, called the Hermetic sciences. <b>There is not much detail given about this world, short of the fact that it exists under a dome of parchment sky due to a demonic curse, and honestly...I just didn't get it. I never felt immersed in the actual setting.</b> The names and places are strange, you have all these Grecian-based names like Damascus and Adamastos and all of a sudden...Lily Martin? What the fuck?<br /><br />The castle itself and the setting are a lot more well done. This book truly runs very parallel to <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> in that regards. We have a magical shifting castle, we have wondrous ballrooms filled with sparkling water. We have ivy-covered libraries. We have a wondrous library, we have a magical wardrobe (I NEED ONE FOR CHRISTMAS), we have invisible hands conjuring up feasts and utensils (except without the singing and dancing, the best part!), we have a forbidden object.<br /><br />But of course, all is not wondrous, and some corners of the castle is filled with horror.<blockquote>
  <i>My fingers found cloth, then something soft and cold.<br />I shuddered, but my mind refused to recognize it until I groped farther and my fingers slid past teeth into a cold, wet mouth.<br /><br />With a scream, I bolted back against the door. I rubbed my hand viciously against my skirt, but the fabric could not wipe away the memory of touching the dead girl’s tongue.<br /><br />The dead wife’s tongue. Because now my eyes were growing truly accustomed to the light, and I could see all eight of them, laid out on their stone blocks as if stored for future use.</i>
</blockquote>Dead wives. Shadowy horrors that drives a person into madness. The castle is equally splendid and sinister.<br /><br /><u>The Characterization</u>: I really liked Nyx. She was frustrating to me at times, but overall, I felt she was a really good, flawed character. Nyx is so, so very angry at the beginning of the novel, and I seethed with anger along with her. She has been dealt a crappy blow by the fates, and who can blame her for her bitterness? Nyx has been doomed since she was born, thanks to her parents' selfishness.<blockquote>
  <i>I hate you [Mother], I prayed silently. Father only bargained for your sake. If you had not been so weak, so desperate, I would not be doomed. I hate you, Mother, forever and ever.</i>
</blockquote>I love a good depiction of sisterly relationships, and Nyx's relationship with her twin sister, Astraia, was so well done. There is absolutely no doubt that Nyx adores her sister while simultaneously hating her as well. Astraia has been adored by everyone since she was born, while her twin sister, Nyx, has been groomed to die. Nyx has lived her life in resentment, and who can blame her for that? Even so, she never, ever shows her bright, innocent sister any hate until she is overwhelmed by her emotions on the day of her wedding...which might as well have been a funeral.<blockquote>
  <i>I had thought the words so often, they felt like nothing in my mouth, like no more than a breath of air, and as easily as breathing I went on:<br />“The truth is, Mother died because of you, and now I have to die for your sake too. And neither one of us will ever forgive you.”<br />Then I shoved her aside and strode out of the room.</i>
</blockquote>Nyx speaks her mind, regrets it immediately, and spends the rest of the book tortured by those final words to her beloved sister.<br /><br />Nyx has spunk, she has fire. Instead of cowering to Ignifex, she turns against him, surprising him and herself...and earns his respect in the process. She hates Ignifex, but Nyx is not a person of absolute cruelty. Despite herself, she is a gentle person, she wants to be more than that girl with hatred in her heart. Despite knowing Ignifex is evil, she finds that she is unable to ignore someone when they are in pain. She is better than that. She wants to be better than that.<blockquote>
  <i>But I was a girl who had broken her sister’s heart and—for a moment—liked it. I had left somebody in torment and liked it.<br />I didn’t want to keep being that person.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Romance</u>: <b>It was well done, but there were entirely way too fucking much of it</b>. As I said above, there were too much romance at the expense of the actual plot. Once Nyx got into the castle, I expected her to plot, to finalize her plan to kill Ignifex. She didn't. She spends her time moping. She spends her time making googly eyes at Shade, then after resisting Ignifex (who is technically her husband), slowly lowers her resistance...then kisses Shade. Then kisses Shade some more. COME ON, YOU'RE SUPPOSED TO BE PLOTTING TO KILL THE EVIL GUY. What pisses me off is that <b>Nyx and her father has a plan to kill Ignifex using Hermetic sciences</b> and she did not follow through except in the most halfhearted way. Instead, this is what we get: <blockquote>
  <i>It was nothing like kissing Shade. That had been like a dream that slowly enfolded me; this was like a battle or a dance. [Ignifex] took possession of my mouth and I took possession of his, and we held each other in a perilous, perfect balance like the circulation of the planets.</i>
</blockquote>Less romance, more plot, please.<br /><br />Thanks to the wonderful Faye for lending me this book.<br /><br /><i>I received this book as an Advance Review Copy; all quotes are taken from an uncorrected galley and is subject to change in the final edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9652936156943143748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1410990601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410990601" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410990601?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=continuations-n-retellings">continuations-n-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=books-everyone-loves-but-me">books-everyone-loves-but-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410990601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7842174637346280045"><i>For one moment, I felt like a river running down to his ocean.</i><br/><br/>i feel like i need to drop a few lines here about what, precisely, i felt was lacking in this story. i so rarely throw down a fewer-than-three-stars rating on here, i figure an explanation may be helpful. i'm not going to go into too much plot-detail, since there are a bazillion reviews of this book already on here - i just want to have a record of my own reaction, for the day when some stranger asks me WHYYYYYYYYYYYY i didn't like th</span>
  <span id="freeText7842174637346280045" style="display:none"><i>For one moment, I felt like a river running down to his ocean.</i><br><br>i feel like i need to drop a few lines here about what, precisely, i felt was lacking in this story. i so rarely throw down a fewer-than-three-stars rating on here, i figure an explanation may be helpful. i'm not going to go into too much plot-detail, since there are a bazillion reviews of this book already on here - i just want to have a record of my own reaction, for the day when some stranger asks me WHYYYYYYYYYYYY i didn't like this. <br><br>there are a few reasons.<br><br>1) i am confused<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444497782i/16509287._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>on paper, the concept of fusing multiple fairytales with classical mythology is exciting and should make for a pleasantly dense story that is at once comfortably familiar but also studded with surprising AHA moments as the overlaps and contrasts begin to manifest. however - there wasn't a true marriage between the elements here. their presence was more decorative than functional, and while it occasionally meshed well, overall it was just too cluttered. it's like when you have a really delicious cupcake and it's already got a tasty frosting on top but then someone thinks "add gummy worms!" and it throws off the texture <i>and</i> the taste and you have to chew SO MUCH you forget about how tasty the cupcake was because you're so focused on not choking to death. <br><br>2) nyx, the heroine of this book and NOT the greek goddess of night (whose name is a bit problematic in a book that incorporates so many other aspects of greek mythology and in which darkness/shadows but not specifically nighttime are a preoccupation) anyway, her. she's meant to be the sacrifice and savior of her people, trained since she was a little girl in both fighting and magical arts and yet she is not at all a badass heroine. once she gets to the castle, she's completely directionless, which makes the book directionless. she's inconsistent, unstable, easily distracted, prone to violent and short-lived outbursts that simmer down into grumbling recriminations directed at multiple targets. it's emotional whiplash - with her sister, she is loving and resentful, protective and hurtful, with ignifex, she goes from attraction to attempted homicide and back again in the blink of an eye. the inconsistency makes it confusing and difficult to root for her to succeed, because it's hard to know what "success" would even look like, with all the cross-purposes and competing goals and obstacles.<br><br>3) <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7uEBuqkkQRk" rel="nofollow noopener">bizarre love triangle</a><br><br>this book is best categorized as a fantasy romance, but i was completely unmoved by the romance itself. which - yes, is a familiar feeling for me, since i'm not a fan of romances, so i'm an easy target for your accusations of not being the right audience. howevs, even when i read a romance that doesn't make me swoon or whatever, i can usually understand why it would work for other readers - i can see that the bones (heh) of the relationship are solid and why the two would fall for each other and why readers would cheer. but this one - this is such a perfunctory romance that exists only because we are told it exists. technically it's a love triangle, and it's at least an interesting <i>version</i> of a love triangle, but it's also the worst kind of instalove because it's unfounded, unearned, and circumstantially selfish. <br><br>those are the big three complaints, and all i can muster as a "review" right now. i still really want to read the second book in this standalone series. i think there's a great story underneath all this clutter and i am really rooting for it to manifest in the second installment. at the very least, i am excited because it's a love story between a monsterfighting girl and a boy with no hands. which is pretty hot. <br><br>************************************************************<br>my guess is that some joker broke into my digital copy of this and gleefully altered its contents; transforming it from the amazing, life-changing book everyone is raving about into some half-baked romance featuring a sloppy and confusing mythos-mashup and completely lacking in either emotional tension or a cohesive narrative.<br><br>this is either some sort of magic eye puzzle i'm just not equipped to "see" or i have forgotten how to read books.<br><br>maybe i'll review this further tomorrow, or maybe i'll take a nap.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7842174637346280045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer9508984111215298321">huh. im really quite shocked. this is the first <i>‘beauty and the beast’</i> retelling that i havent enjoyed. ive read and loved so many, so for me to not click with this is a major disappointment. <br/><br/>i appreciate the unique spin on a classic story, but i found the pacing to be slow, the writing to be dull and repetitious, the characters to be unlikable, and the world-building to be confusing and out of place. there really wasnt much that i liked about this, to be honest, and im super jealous of all the </span>
  <span id="freeText9508984111215298321" style="display:none">huh. im really quite shocked. this is the first <i>‘beauty and the beast’</i> retelling that i havent enjoyed. ive read and loved so many, so for me to not click with this is a major disappointment. <br /><br />i appreciate the unique spin on a classic story, but i found the pacing to be slow, the writing to be dull and repetitious, the characters to be unlikable, and the world-building to be confusing and out of place. there really wasnt much that i liked about this, to be honest, and im super jealous of all the readers who fell head over heels for this. <br /><br />maybe this authors particular storytelling/style just isnt for me. :/<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>2 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2905840552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2905840552?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062224743" href="/book/show/22693181-cruel-beauty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=love-to-hate-and-hate-to-love">love-to-hate-and-hate-to-love</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=low-or-no-steam">low-or-no-steam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=clear-my-bookshelf-challenge">clear-my-bookshelf-challenge</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2905840552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7079263189782354762"><b>3.25 - 3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Last night I got a bee up my ass and decided to count and see how many unread physical books I have on my home library shelves...and let’s just say the number was pretty shameful. <br/><br/>Thus, I decided it was time to cull the herd. So decided I would try the cliched booktube trend of reading first chapters of books that have been on my shelves awhile...unhauling anything that didn’t at least mildly capture my attention. <br/><br/>This book has been on my shelves the longest, so I grabbed it and </span>
  <span id="freeText7079263189782354762" style="display:none"><b>3.25 - 3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Last night I got a bee up my ass and decided to count and see how many unread physical books I have on my home library shelves...and let’s just say the number was pretty shameful. <br /><br />Thus, I decided it was time to cull the herd. So decided I would try the cliched booktube trend of reading first chapters of books that have been on my shelves awhile...unhauling anything that didn’t at least mildly capture my attention. <br /><br />This book has been on my shelves the longest, so I grabbed it and figured I’d read one chapter and set it aside in the donate pile...342 pages later, I can proudly say I unhauled one fucking book. But it’s now a "read" book. So nanner nanner nanner. <br /><br />I really enjoyed certain elements of this story and was (obviously) drawn in from the very first page. I thought the ending got a little dicey as far as plot details and general continuity is concerned...And I feel like the romance/love was never truly cemented enough for my tastes...but all in all a decent story I’m glad I read...<br /><br />If only so I can say I read a book from my shelves I had started to think I never would get to. A truly satisfying feeling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7079263189782354762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3983594012234996003" style="display:none">I loved the first 100 pages of this book so much that i was 99% sure it'd be a 4 or 5 star book. I loved the writing and the main character's sass, and the "Dark Lord" or whatever his title is was REALLY interesting. But holy moly, this book does a 180. It starts out strong but turns into trash. I'm still roiling a bit on what just happened there at the end because it also starts to pull in time travle???? literaly??/ what ??????<br /><br /> I will not be continuing this series and I would not recommend this one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6507369954014153384">I have to give the narrator, Elizabeth Knowelden, some credit here. She tried. She really, really tried to salvage this book by giving the main character tons of personality, but not even she could change the source material. The fact is that <em>Cruel Beauty</em> made absolutely no damn sense.<br/><br/>How does the magic work? I dunno.<br/><br/>Who are the real bad guys? I dunno.<br/><br/>Wait, what's the SECRET. Well, I dunno because Nyx learns it and then FORGETS it on the next page to conveniently keep the plot rolling. Awesome.<br/><br/>H</span>
  <span id="freeText6507369954014153384" style="display:none">I have to give the narrator, Elizabeth Knowelden, some credit here. She tried. She really, really tried to salvage this book by giving the main character tons of personality, but not even she could change the source material. The fact is that <em>Cruel Beauty</em> made absolutely no damn sense.<br /><br />How does the magic work? I dunno.<br /><br />Who are the real bad guys? I dunno.<br /><br />Wait, what's the SECRET. Well, I dunno because Nyx learns it and then FORGETS it on the next page to conveniently keep the plot rolling. Awesome.<br /><br />HUH? There's time travel? ....Maybe, but not really. It's a SECRET that you'll never find out and/or stop caring about.<br /><br /><em>Cruel Beauty</em> was like a mixing pot of great ideas that didn't get mixed very well. The oil rose to the top and the cake fell flat. Also, I have no idea what the hell I'm talking about, kinda like this book. But the narrator's voice was nice.</span>

سرعان ما تحولت معي لقصة مملة ومضجرة<br>ربما هي رغبة البطلة هنا في "البصق" علي كل من تقابله وغضبها وضجرها الدائم اصابني بالعدوي فلم احتمل البطء في منتصف الاحداث<br>ربما هو الحب المبالغ به في وصفه -كعادة الروايات الشبابية<br>InstaLove<br>والذي حولها من بطلة غاضبة قاسية الي بطلة غاضبة قاسية بلهاء ومملة بالاخص بعلاقة الحب الثلاثية المعتادة<br><br>لكني لا انكر ان الجزء الممل بالمنتصف وحتي قبل الربع الاخير كان به الكثير من الايجابيات، المزج الساحر للميثولوجيا الاغريقية كصندوق بندورا، كيوبيد وتوم الوحيد وغيرها جعل الامر مثيرا<br><br>ولكني ظللت بسبب التطويل هنا أشعر انها رواية متوسطة، نجمتان ونصف علي الاكثر<br><br>ثم جاء الربع الاخير<br>والذي بدأ ببعض اللمحات من التشابهة بين احداث القصة وقصة "الجميلة والوحش" التي جاءت بذكاء بشكل مختلف عن الاصل متشابه في الهيكل فقط ايضا كان ممتعا<br>ثم انقلبت القصة بمفاجأت وتلاعب بديع بالزمن لتتحول لقصة مختلفة تماما<br>لتأتي<br><br><u>النهـــايـة</u><br>والتي كما قالت من رشحت لي الرواية بذكاء أنها مفتاح الرواية<br>المفتاح الذي قد يجعل لكل الاحداث التي قد تكون مملة احيانا ، لكل الغضب مستمر، لكل قصة حب لها قيمة ولها معني<br><br>قصة يتضافر فيها الحب، والقسوة والتضحية بشكل ممتاز بل ويظهر "مورال" الحكاية بشكل واضح ولكن غير مباشر بنفس الوقت<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487957471ra/22068463.gif" width="400" height="222" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>بالربع الاخير ستدرك أن الطبيعة البشرية بها الجمال وبها القسوة لاسباب <br>هي قصة المتناقضات البشرية..الحب والواجب، القسوة والتعاطف<br>طبيعة البشر في الامنيات..الامنيات التي لا نعرف ثمنها الا عندما تتحقق<br><br>لم اتخيل ابدا تلك النهاية الساحرة، ولا مدي قسوتي علي الفكرة الرائعة للرواية <br><i>نعم مازلت اري ان يعيبها التطويل بمنتصفها لكن يكفي انتقاص نجمة واحدة لهذا</i><br><br>إعادة حكي تستحق القراءة</b><br><i>قبل اعادة فيلم الجميلة والوحش قريبا</i><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><b>Mini English Review</b><br>-----------------<blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487932598ra/22065259.gif" width="400" height="487" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Well, I loved the beginning...promising of Dark, Cruel Beauty and the Beast retelling..<br>mind the spitful, cruel, protagonist that in need for a serious 'Anger Management'..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487948260ra/22067413.gif" width="400" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>-not the beast, nope..the girl actually made me really angry most of the time-</i><br>Oh and don't expect that since she's the cruel angry one here she'd marry a gentle-beast..nooo, he's like Lucifer himself.<br><br>Well, this 'angry' bride, full of hatred.. is destined since she was very young to marry a monster.<br>And as most YAs...she will fall in love with him..., and <i>again, as most YAs</i>, she have feelings for his servant, his <i>Shadow</i>, Shade.<br><br>So..the story after the strong introduction and good setting, turned fast to feminine dull slow rant...with Love Triangle.., It was as boring as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a>, and bit of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21524446.A_Thousand_Nights__A_Thousand_Nights___1_" title="A Thousand Nights (A Thousand Nights, #1) by E.K. Johnston" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Nights</a>'s dryness..<br>But it was only adorned with Greek mythology every now and then that made me feel better.. some real myths like Pandora's Box myth, and some strange as Nanny-Anna and Tom-Alone..<br><br>But still , I felt bored in the middle many times... wanna spit as the protagonist having the same urge to spit on everyone.<br><br><br>But the concept of the myth of "Kindly One", and the wishes, the barging of the Gentle lord is amazing..<br>That was an interesting plot here, people can't understand actually what they wish for...<br>That their wishes has a price..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487791605ra/22051775.gif" width="400" height="224" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND then comes the strong last few chapters and the end.. and what an ending... ONE OF THE BEST ENDINGS I've ever read.<br>Where the moral of this Cruel Story, the contradictions of human nature, how the cruelty is compassion and how we never understand what we wish for..<br>How there's no pure good...no pure evil.<br><br>God, I just loved the ending...and appreciate the story much more than I expected..<br><br>It's a retelling that worth the reading really.<br><br>Mohanmed Arabey<br>From 14 Feb. 2017<br>To 17 Feb. 2017<br><br><i><a href="http://vivus1999.deviantart.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">illustrator of the art </a>at the beginning of the review</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2018314855621551893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer506251208801837518">I'm not sure of what to think of this book... I really loved it... but at the same time I didn´t? Let me try to arrange my thoughts... <br/><br/>I was very excited about this book, so I was a little dissappointed because I wasn't really digging it and I was already at page 100... but after that it really became really really good! I started to like the characters and I kinda fell in love with the Gentle Lord, Ignifex <3. <br/><br/>I think that I wasn't liking it at the begining because Nyx is always changing her mi</span>
  <span id="freeText506251208801837518" style="display:none">I'm not sure of what to think of this book... I really loved it... but at the same time I didn´t? Let me try to arrange my thoughts... <br /><br />I was very excited about this book, so I was a little dissappointed because I wasn't really digging it and I was already at page 100... but after that it really became really really good! I started to like the characters and I kinda fell in love with the Gentle Lord, Ignifex &lt;3. <br /><br />I think that I wasn't liking it at the begining because Nyx is always changing her mind and I wanted to slap her sometimes, but also because the world in this book is really confusing! At first I didn't understand a thing about the "Hermetic" laws and the elemental hearts, then it became clearer, but we also had demons, gods, "kindly ones", shadows, mithology, fantasy, and so much more that I don't think I fully understood the world at the end of the book, but that doesn't mean I didn't like it, on the contrary, I found it very interesting! <br /><br />I decided to give this book 4 stars because of the slow begining and because of what I said in the paragraph above, but those were the only things I didn't really like... I just loved Ignifex so much, the way he loved and trusted Nyx &lt;3. Also, I thought his back story was amazing! A true mistery and at the end when we learn what really happened it blew my mind! <br /><br />Really, I devoured the second half of this book! And I nearly cried because of the destiny of Nyx and Ignifex :(. It was so unfair! UGH. About the ending... I'm kinda torn. I didn't expected it and I like that, also, I think it was sweet and overall, a good ending, but I don't know, I feel like I didn't fully understood what happened (again, because the world and the demons and the gods were so confusing)...<br /><br />I'm satisfied with it, that's for sure, and I got a little book hangover! That was also unexpected! When I finished the book I couldn't stop thinking about Nyx and Ignifex and the magical world of Arcadia.<br /><br />OH, and I can't go without saying that one of the things I loved the most of this book was THE CASTLE. I LOVED IT COMPLETELY. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666075041" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/666075041?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=creeeeepy">creeeeepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=this-book-and-i-are-eloping">this-book-and-i-are-eloping</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-e-i-will-always-love-you">i-e-i-will-always-love-you</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer666075041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9805743473330129245">Let me say it now: <i>Cruel Beauty</i> is one fantastic, gorgeously written, spectacularly dark debut. Many of its aspects may not appeal to some readers, and I understand that; although I really loved how the romance in <i>Cruel Beauty</i> and the "love triangle" (note the quotation marks--don't run off) played out, I do understand why some other readers, a handful of my friends amongst them, take issue with much of this novel. <br/><br/>But honestly, it's been over a week since I've finished <i>Cruel Beauty</i>, and I have </span>
  <span id="freeText9805743473330129245" style="display:none">Let me say it now: <i>Cruel Beauty</i> is one fantastic, gorgeously written, spectacularly dark debut. Many of its aspects may not appeal to some readers, and I understand that; although I really loved how the romance in <i>Cruel Beauty</i> and the "love triangle" (note the quotation marks--don't run off) played out, I do understand why some other readers, a handful of my friends amongst them, take issue with much of this novel. <br /><br />But honestly, it's been over a week since I've finished <i>Cruel Beauty</i>, and I have truly nothing negative to say about it, other than the fact that the world-building and terminology may be a bit overwhelming at first. However, when I got accustomed to the world in <i>Cruel Beauty</i>, and got a grasp on where Hodge was going with the story around fifty pages in, I was absolute putty in this book's hand. <br /><br /><i>Cruel Beauty</i> is a very ambitious novel, and it's one that will likely throw some readers off in how odd it is; it's a Beauty and the Beast retelling, with some Greek mythology thrown in, a whole lot of fantasy, a maybe even a hint of dystopian aspects, and trust me when I say it's all handled really, really well. What could have easily been a convoluted and silly novel instead incorporated each and every one of those aforementioned plot points seamlessly. <br /><br />Nyx is a strong willed character, and is at times a bit frustrating, but she is also one of the most realistic characters I've read about this year. After all the things she goes through in the novel, she's understandably angry and fickle regarding whom she truly loves, and why. In reality, I think anyone would react similar to how Nyx reacted if they were placed in the same situation as her. As well as being an authentic character, she does eventually grow past the anger that was so evidently boiling up inside her in the beginning of the novel, but she never truly gets past it, much like anyone wouldn't. And that's why I love her character arc and development: you may be just as frustrated as Nyx is with her anger and fickleness, but you can't deny that her emotions are <i>real</i>, and you'd react the same. In any other novel, with any other character, Nyx's actions may just have annoyed me. I'm aware of this; but in <i>Cruel Beauty</i>, Rosamund Hodge creates a character in Nyx that is, while not always likable, wholly relatable, and that is a great feat in my eyes. <br /><br />And then there's Ignifex, who is one charming little bastard, and I'll leave it at that. There are much more things for me to touch upon in regards to the romance in this novel, all of which are spoilers. So I'm just going to let the readers of this unravel the mysteries of this romance on their own. (And trust me, it's something you'll want to discover on your own. The romance is something you'll either love or hate (see below), but it is definitely intriguing and original.) But yes, Ignifex--awesome, complex character, with a unique and surprising backstory...yes. Yes, yes, yes. Lovers of Cole from the <i>Everneath</i> series by Brodi Ashton, this guy's for you. <br /><br />I think <i>Cruel Beauty</i> is a novel that will have some pretty contrasting opinions once it's published. Although some think its romance is insta-love (which I disagree with since it was said that five months passed before any 'love' thoughts occurred, but I digress) with an unnecessary love triangle (which I also respectfully disagree with because of <i>reasons</i>, but you all know how I feel about love triangles), I found <i>Cruel Beauty</i> to be a truly beautiful and stunningly original debut. With it, Rosamund Hodge has taken some aspects from Beauty and the Beast that manage to make the novel stand out as an adaptation, but she also introduces so many new concepts of her own to make the ageless tale as old as time we all love even lovelier. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9805743473330129245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_925915379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/925915379" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/925915379?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Beauty and the Beast</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=wow">wow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=uncommon">uncommon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=not-what-i-expected">not-what-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=smart-heroine">smart-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer925915379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11494799941846600666"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398980467i/9492797._SX540_.jpg' width='500' height='280' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>4 ''Wow, that was some story!'' stars</b><br/><br/>Why haven’t I read this book sooner? *Ashamed of herself*<br/><br/>First of all, I do not agree with the average rating of 3.80/5 stars on Goodreads. At all. It actually happens pretty rarely that I don’t, but I definitely think that <i>Cruel Beauty</i> deserves a higher one and also much more attention. Much more. <br/><br/><i>Cruel Beauty</i> made me reconsider many things I thought I knew about myself regarding books. For example, I don’t like slow-paced books. Is this a book with slow-pac</span>
  <span id="freeText11494799941846600666" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398980467i/9492797._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4 ''Wow, that was some story!'' stars</b><br><br>Why haven’t I read this book sooner? *Ashamed of herself*<br><br>First of all, I do not agree with the average rating of 3.80/5 stars on Goodreads. At all. It actually happens pretty rarely that I don’t, but I definitely think that <i>Cruel Beauty</i> deserves a higher one and also much more attention. Much more. <br><br><i>Cruel Beauty</i> made me reconsider many things I thought I knew about myself regarding books. For example, I don’t like slow-paced books. Is this a book with slow-paced writing? Yes, it is, and I didn’t even mind its slowness a bit. If you’re not a fan of slow-paced books, I can’t tell to avoid this one because, hey, I loved it! The beginning is indeed a little too extended but don’t give up yet and give the book a chance!<br><br><b>The story:</b> I was incredibly curious about this one when I discovered it on Goodreads not so long ago (thank you GR!) because some reviewers said it was a remarkable retelling of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> and some others actually said that they didn’t see much of the fairy tale in it. I saw a lot of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> in the story myself and especially as background like the vast library of the castle, its labyrinth halls, the invisible servants, etc. <br><br>It is narrated with a first person POV. I never had a problem with first or third person POV and this one is no exception. The story starts on Nyx, living her last moments at her house with her father, twin sister and aunt. It was obvious that she wasn’t as close as people normally are to their family and relatives and it intrigued me. I was craving to know why and where did all the hate come from. From the first sentence, I was hooked and was sure <i>Cruel Beauty</i> was going to be something unlikely everything I have ever read. And I didn’t even have high expectations. Nyx had many various and contradicted feelings towards her sister especially because of her objective towards the Gentle Lord (quite an interesting name for the demon Lord). She was scared and angry. I could understand her every feeling and the fact that it mustn’t be easy for her to be the one on which such a responsibility is held. She is the chosen one, the one who has to kill the Lord and free their country from demons. Nyx is brave and strong and a survivor. That’s how I like my heroines to be. Sometimes she really needed to think before she spoke though, because I was a bit annoyed of her always regretting her impulsive words afterwards. I liked her from the very beginning still and it didn’t change throughout the story. She’s human; everyone messes up when emotions are involved, something I think every one can understand.<br><br><b>The world-building:</b> Original and unique. With it, the story felt even more important, riveting and captivating. It captivated me to a point that I wasn’t expecting or prepared to. There should’ve been a warning ‘’Prepare to be captivated’’ on the cover. Everything was well detailed and described. Although, the castle wasn’t at all was I imagined it to be. I was imagining it to be quite dark with an eerie atmosphere and not one that made me think of a strange, uncommon house. Some walls are in blue color for example and some have fruits and flower prints. I mean, come on…So yeah, I did cringe my teeth for a bit while reading those descriptions. It marked me and deceived me at first, because I really had an image of the castle in my head thanks to the cover. When I passed that surprised and just played along (more like made an abstraction of it), I started being more fascinated by all the discoveries Nyx made in the castle. All the secret rooms waiting to be open got my attention and I just wished I was Nyx so I could fulfill my avid curiosity. <i>Cruel Beauty</i> definitely has a special and an interesting world-building worth reading about and paying attention to.<br><br><b>The writing:</b> As I said, the story is slow-paced but not the boring and <i>oh-my-gosh-seriously-is-it-going-to-end-someday</i> kind. If you usually don’t like slow-paced book, I would still say try it because exceptions always exist and this was one of them for me. Also, the writing was very pretty, beautiful, and admiring. I like when I’m able to learn new words while reading a book and in YAs, I don’t very often have the chance. With this one I absolutely had and I’ve learned some quite complex words. It was obvious that the author, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6474354.Rosamund_Hodge" title="Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosamund Hodge</a>, wrote her story carefully, trying to make it as perfect and as rich as she was able to. And she succeeded. It was amazing! Everything was perfectly detailed with the right amount of details which made easy to picture the characters and the surroundings/setting. Another small complaint I would make is that, in the first chapters, Nyx wasn’t described enough which made it hard to really connect with her at the beginning of the story. Fortunately, the secondary characters were indeed some interesting ones so it finally didn’t bother me that much. Although, I did notice. I didn’t feel like there was a single kind of atmosphere, more like a combination of a calm, ‘’on edge’’, mysterious and by moment eerie too.<br><br><b>The romance:</b> I was willing to give this book five big shinny well deserved stars, before the love triangle became really present and annoying. I usually actually don’t mind love triangles that much (depending on the intensity) but this one was one of the worst I have ever read about. Mainly because it made the strong and smart heroine (Nyx) look weak and pathetic by moments. Also, the romance was very very rushed. They were loving each other already a couple of days after they met. Indeed, there were some cute moments remarquably well developed (it wasn’t all bad) but, most of the time, I was just plain bored. <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retellings shouldn’t, in my opinion have such love triangles ever again. I won’t say which characters were in the love triangle because I think it’s best that you discover it by yourself and I don’t want to spoil it for you.<br><br><b>Overall:</b> I think I’ve already use way too many adjectives for this book in this review, so I will simply say that it impressed me and did take my breath away at the beginning of the story. So, if you would like to read a fabulous fantasy story like you have never read before with unforgettable characters, a predictable but nice romance with a love triangle and a well thought plot that will leave you only wanting for more, I would recommend you <i>Cruel Beauty</i> with no hesitation. <br><br>Happy reading!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11494799941846600666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regan" href="/user/show/19645927-regan">Regan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer860053176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13207611674302452978">This book really surprised me. <br/><br/>When I was first reading this book I was not really digging it, I thought I had a handle on where the story was going, and therefore I thought it was too predictable. However, this story did not follow the stereotypical path that I thought it would. I still guessed the ending halfway in, but I enjoyed the ride nonetheless. The amount of predictability that may or may not be present in this book is not the important part, no, the important part is the story. The sto</span>
  <span id="freeText13207611674302452978" style="display:none">This book really surprised me. <br /><br />When I was first reading this book I was not really digging it, I thought I had a handle on where the story was going, and therefore I thought it was too predictable. However, this story did not follow the stereotypical path that I thought it would. I still guessed the ending halfway in, but I enjoyed the ride nonetheless. The amount of predictability that may or may not be present in this book is not the important part, no, the important part is the story. The story is what really kept me so interested, it was beautiful and unique, and the delivery could not be ignored. The world combined well known ancient lore with (made up?) reinterpretations that added a wonderful level of fantasy. It was whimsical, and I really fell in love with the characters. I enjoyed throughly that they recognized their flaws and accepted them. The last 30 pages or so is what made me write this whole review because I LOVED the ending. So much. This book delivered something I did not expect, so for that I tip my hat to it. <br /><br />Also, it's a standalone. Score. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13207611674302452978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621126440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6118529168488864526">I realize that this book doesn't come out for quite a while, but as soon as it downloaded on my Kindle, I started reading it right away, and once I'd finished it, there was no holding back the feels.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380422418ra/840437.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><b>This book is amazering.</b><br/><br/><br/>It's half:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380422418ra/840438.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>And another half:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422418i/840439.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>And considering Beauty and the Beast is one of my favorite Disney movies/fairy tales and the Cupid and Psyche myth is probably my favorite in the entire Greek mythology canon...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/584507.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>This book has some of the coolest worldbuilding I've seen in a YA novel. O</span>
  <span id="freeText6118529168488864526" style="display:none">I realize that this book doesn't come out for quite a while, but as soon as it downloaded on my Kindle, I started reading it right away, and once I'd finished it, there was no holding back the feels.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380422418ra/840437.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>This book is amazering.</b><br><br><br>It's half:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380422418ra/840438.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And another half:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422418i/840439.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And considering Beauty and the Beast is one of my favorite Disney movies/fairy tales and the Cupid and Psyche myth is probably my favorite in the entire Greek mythology canon...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/584507.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This book has some of the coolest worldbuilding I've seen in a YA novel. Originally, I thought the book was going to be high fantasy, but now I'm not so sure. It almost feels like "low," or "second world" fantasy, as the setting is a world that was settled by the Greeks and then cut off from the rest of the world. For that reason, the people believe in Greek gods, and the demons that the blurb refers to are supposed to have originated in Tartarus.<br><br>The mythology spin on the story was a total surprise, as the blurb doesn't mention it, and I found myself even more excited in the first couple chapters because of it. I also saw an interview with Rosamund Hodge on Epic Reads, where she said that her story is based just as much on the Cupid and Psyche myth as it is on Beauty and the Beast (if not more), so I'm not sure why the myth bit isn't in the blurb. It should be, IMHO.<br><br>Okay, so let's talk about characters. Holy shiz. These characters are so crazy and dark and totally different than most other YA protagonists. Nyx is what I wanted Rose Hathaway from <i>Vampire Academy</i> to be - BA and mean, with an iron will, but so broken that you couldn't help but love her. I loved how her family relationships pushed her into her feelings for Ignifex. Her character motivation and development flowed really well, I thought.<br><br>Ignifex is also pretty amazing. He reminded me of all those Victorian anti-heroes that are more wicked than good, like Heathcliff. Or maybe like the selfish gods of mythology that have to learn compassion. Either way, I enjoyed his development a lot too, and although I figured out early on the big twist about his identity, just like with <i>Cinder</i> by Marissa Meyer, I didn't care.<br><br>I was totally absorbed in this book. I couldn't put it down. Basically, this was me and Cruel Beauty:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380422418ra/840440.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And when people tried to talk to me:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380422418ra/840441.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Okay, and the end.<br><br><b>THE END!!!</b><br><br>*shakes computer*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/564900.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Loved it, loved it!<br><br>I won't say anything else.<br><br>Just know.<br><br>It's amazing.<br><br>I know it's terribly CRUEL of me (see what I did there?) to tell you all these lovely things about this book when it doesn't release until January. I'm very sorry. But go ahead and add it to your Goodreads TBR list now, because YOU NEED THIS BOOK IN YOUR LIFE! It's dark and twisted and original and wonderful. There's fabulous worldbuilding, seriously messed up characters that Rosamund Hodge makes you love, and some really vivid imagery that I didn't talk about before but is also really great.<br><br><br>GO BUY THIS BOOK!<br>...IN JANUARY!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6118529168488864526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
